As the only state-funded historically black university in the state, TSU plays a vital role in providing accessible and high-quality education across diverse disciplines.</p><p>The university offers a broad array of programs, including <strong>41 bachelor’s degrees</strong>, <strong>23 master’s degrees, </strong>and <strong>8 doctoral degrees</strong>. TSU is classified as a "<strong>Doctoral University with High Research Activity</strong>" by the Carnegie Classification, reflecting its robust research contributions. The campus spans 500 acres and houses over <strong>65 </strong>buildings, making it the largest college campus in Nashville. TSU offers a range of on-campus housing options, including dormitories and apartment complexes, ensuring students have a comfortable living experience.</p><p>Student life at TSU is dynamic, with more than <strong>60 </strong>registered student organizations, including the <strong>Student Government Association </strong>and the <strong>Aristocrat of Bands</strong>. Athletics play a key role at TSU, with the university competing in <strong>NCAA Division I </strong>as a member of the <strong>Ohio Valley Conference</strong>.</p><p>In 2024, TSU celebrated a milestone, surpassing <strong>$100 million in research funding</strong>, solidifying its position as a leader among historically black colleges and universities (HBCUs). Through its commitment to academic excellence, cutting-edge research, and community engagement, TSU remains a cornerstone of higher education in Tennessee and beyond.</p><p>Living near Tennessee University provides easy access to universities, local amenities, and a vibrant student community.
